<p><b>Google Search</b> (also known simply as <b>Google</b> or <b>google.com</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>. It allows users to search for information on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">Web</a> by entering keywords or phrases. Google Search uses <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithms</a> to analyze and rank <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">websites</a> based on their relevance to the search query. Google Search is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-visited_websites" title="List of most-visited websites">most-visited website in the world</a>. As of 2025, Google Search has a 90% share of the global search engine market.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Approximately 24.1% of Google's monthly global traffic comes from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, 5.6% from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, 5.5% from <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, 4.8% from <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, and 3.7% from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> according to data provided by <a href="/wiki/Similarweb" title="Similarweb">Similarweb</a>. The same source reports that 58% of users are male and 42% are female.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The order of search results returned by Google is based, in part, on a priority rank system called "<a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank</a>". Google Search also provides many different options for customized searches, using symbols to include, exclude, specify or require certain search behavior, and offers specialized interactive experiences, such as flight status and package tracking, weather forecasts, currency, unit, and time conversions, word definitions, and more.
</p><p>The main purpose of Google Search is to search for text in publicly accessible documents offered by web servers, as opposed to other data, such as <a href="/wiki/Image_search" class="mw-redirect" title="Image search">images</a> or <a href="/wiki/Database_search_engine" title="Database search engine">data contained in databases</a>. It was originally developed in 1996 by <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Hassan" title="Scott Hassan">Scott Hassan</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-vanityfair&#95;5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanityfair-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The search engine would also be set up in the garage of <a href="/wiki/Susan_Wojcicki" title="Susan Wojcicki">Susan Wojcicki</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">Menlo Park</a> home.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2011, Google introduced "<a href="/wiki/Google_Voice_Search" title="Google Voice Search">Google Voice Search</a>" to search for spoken, rather than typed, words.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Official&#95;announcement&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Official_announcement-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2012, Google introduced a <a href="/wiki/Semantic_search" title="Semantic search">semantic search</a> feature named <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Graph_(Google)" title="Knowledge Graph (Google)">Knowledge Graph</a>.
</p><p>Analysis of the frequency of search terms may indicate economic, social and health trends.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Pulse&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pulse-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Data about the frequency of use of search terms on Google can be <a href="/wiki/Open_data" title="Open data">openly</a> inquired via <a href="/wiki/Google_Trends" title="Google Trends">Google Trends</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Flu_Trends" title="Google Flu Trends">have been shown to correlate</a> with <a href="/wiki/Flu" class="mw-redirect" title="Flu">flu</a> outbreaks and unemployment levels, and provide the information faster than traditional reporting methods and surveys. As of mid-2016, Google's search engine has begun to rely on <a href="/wiki/Deep_learning#Deep_neural_networks" title="Deep learning">deep neural networks</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2024, a US judge in Virginia ruled that Google held an <a href="/wiki/Monopoly" title="Monopoly">illegal monopoly</a> over Internet search and search advertising.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-The&#95;Economist&#95;13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The court found that Google maintained its market dominance by paying large amounts to phone-makers and browser-developers to make Google its default search engine.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-The&#95;Economist&#95;13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2025, the trial to determine which remedies sought by the Department of Justice would be imposed to address Google's illegal monopoly, which could include breaking up the company and preventing it from using its data to secure dominance in the AI sector.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the court case has passed. (May 2025)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Search_indexing">Search indexing</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Googlebot" title="Googlebot">Googlebot</a></div><p>Google <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_indexing" title="Search engine indexing">indexes</a> hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" class="mw-redirect" title="Terabyte">terabytes</a> of information from <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web pages</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Seeker&#95;indexing&#95;15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seeker_indexing-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before 2024,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google also provided desktop users links to <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_cache" title="Search engine cache">cached</a> versions of their search results, formed by the search engine's latest indexing of the <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">website</a> in question.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Additionally, Google indexes some file types, being able to show users <a href="/wiki/Portable_Document_Format" class="mw-redirect" title="Portable Document Format">PDFs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Word_document" class="mw-redirect" title="Word document">Word documents</a>, <a href="/wiki/Excel_spreadsheet" class="mw-redirect" title="Excel spreadsheet">Excel spreadsheets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_PowerPoint" title="Microsoft PowerPoint">PowerPoint presentations</a>, certain <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Flash multimedia content</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plain_text" title="Plain text">plain text</a> files.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users can also activate "<a href="/wiki/SafeSearch" title="SafeSearch">SafeSearch</a>", a filtering technology aimed at preventing explicit and pornographic content from appearing in search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Despite Google search's immense index, sources generally assume that Google is only indexing less than 5% of the total Internet, with the rest belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Deep_web" title="Deep web">deep web</a>, inaccessible through its search tools.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Seeker&#95;indexing&#95;15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seeker_indexing-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Google changed its search indexing tools to demote sites that had been accused of <a href="/wiki/Online_piracy" title="Online piracy">piracy</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2016, Gary Illyes, a webmaster trends analyst with Google, announced that the search engine would be making a separate, primary web index dedicated for mobile devices, with a secondary, less up-to-date index for desktop use. The change was a response to the continued growth in mobile usage, and a push for web developers to adopt a mobile-friendly version of their websites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In December 2017, Google began rolling out the change, having already done so for multiple websites.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;Caffeine&quot;_search_architecture_upgrade"><span id=".22Caffeine.22_search_architecture_upgrade"></span>"Caffeine" search architecture upgrade</h3></div>
<p>In August 2009, Google invited web developers to test a new search architecture, codenamed "Caffeine", and give their feedback. The new architecture provided no visual differences in the user interface, but added significant speed improvements and a new "under-the-hood" indexing infrastructure. The move was interpreted in some quarters as a response to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s recent release of an upgraded version of its own search service, renamed <a href="/wiki/Bing_(search_engine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bing (search engine)">Bing</a>, as well as the launch of <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Alpha" class="mw-redirect" title="Wolfram Alpha">Wolfram Alpha</a>, a new search engine based on "computational knowledge".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google announced completion of "Caffeine" on June 8, 2010, claiming 50% fresher results due to continuous updating of its index.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With "Caffeine", Google moved its back-end indexing system away from <a href="/wiki/MapReduce" title="MapReduce">MapReduce</a> and onto <a href="/wiki/Bigtable" title="Bigtable">Bigtable</a>, the company's distributed database platform.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;Medic&quot;_search_algorithm_update"><span id=".22Medic.22_search_algorithm_update"></span>"Medic" search algorithm update</h3></div>
<p>In August 2018, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Sullivan_(technologist)" title="Danny Sullivan (technologist)">Danny Sullivan</a> from Google announced a broad core algorithm update. As per current analysis done by the industry leaders Search Engine Watch and Search Engine Land, the update was to drop down the medical and health-related websites that were not user friendly and were not providing good user experience. This is why the industry experts named it "Medic".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Google reserves very high standards for YMYL (Your Money or Your Life) pages. This is because misinformation can affect users financially, physically, or emotionally. Therefore, the update targeted particularly those YMYL pages that have low-quality content and misinformation. This resulted in the algorithm targeting health and medical-related websites more than others. However, many other websites from other industries were also negatively affected.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Search_results">Search results</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ranking_of_results">Ranking of results</h3></div>
<p>By 2012, it handled more than 3.5 billion searches per day.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2013 the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> found that Google Search favored Google's own products, instead of the best result for consumers' needs.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In February 2015 Google announced a major change to its mobile search <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithm</a> which would favor mobile friendly over other <a href="/wiki/Websites" class="mw-redirect" title="Websites">websites</a>. Nearly 60% of Google <a href="/wiki/Online_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Online traffic">searches</a> come from mobile phones. Google says it wants users to have access to premium quality <a href="/wiki/Websites" class="mw-redirect" title="Websites">websites</a>. Those websites which lack a mobile-friendly <a href="/wiki/Interface_(computing)" title="Interface (computing)">interface</a> would be ranked lower and it is expected that this update will cause a shake-up of <a href="/wiki/Page_rank" class="mw-redirect" title="Page rank">ranks</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="Has it? (February 2026)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Businesses who fail to update their <a href="/wiki/Websites" class="mw-redirect" title="Websites">websites</a> accordingly could see a dip in their regular websites traffic.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="PageRank">PageRank</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank</a></div>
<p>Google's rise was largely due to a patented <a href="/wiki/Algorithm" title="Algorithm">algorithm</a> called PageRank which helps rank web pages that match a given search string.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> When Google was a Stanford research project, it was nicknamed <a href="/wiki/BackRub" class="mw-redirect" title="BackRub">BackRub</a> because the technology checks <a href="/wiki/Backlinks" class="mw-redirect" title="Backlinks">backlinks</a> to determine a site's importance. Other keyword-based methods to rank search results, used by many search engines that were once more popular than Google, would check how often the search terms occurred in a page, or how strongly associated the search terms were within each resulting page. The PageRank algorithm instead analyzes human-generated <a href="/wiki/Hyperlink" title="Hyperlink">links</a> assuming that web pages linked from many important pages are also important. The algorithm computes a <a href="/wiki/Recursion" title="Recursion">recursive</a> score for pages, based on the weighted sum of other pages linking to them. PageRank is thought to <a href="/wiki/Correlation" title="Correlation">correlate</a> well with human concepts of importance. In addition to PageRank, Google, over the years, has added many other secret criteria for determining the ranking of resulting pages. This is reported to comprise over 250 different indicators,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the specifics of which are kept secret to avoid difficulties created by scammers and help Google maintain an edge over its competitors globally.
</p><p>PageRank was influenced by a similar page-ranking and site-scoring algorithm earlier used for <a href="/wiki/RankDex" class="mw-redirect" title="RankDex">RankDex</a>, developed by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a> in 1996. Larry Page's patent for PageRank filed in 1998 includes a citation to Li's earlier patent. Li later went on to create the Chinese search engine <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a> in 2000.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In a potential hint of Google's future direction of their Search algorithm, Google's then chief executive <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a>, said in a 2007 interview with the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i>: "The goal is to enable Google users to be able to ask the question such as 'What shall I do tomorrow?' and 'What job shall I take?<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Schmidt reaffirmed this during a 2010 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>: "I actually think most people don't want Google to answer their questions, they want Google to tell them what they should be doing next."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Google_optimization">Google optimization</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_optimization" title="Search engine optimization">Search engine optimization</a></div>
<p>Because Google is the most popular <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Web search engine">search engine</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Webmaster" title="Webmaster">webmasters</a> attempt to influence their website's Google rankings. An industry of consultants has arisen to help websites increase their rankings on Google and other search engines. This field, called search engine optimization, attempts to discern patterns in search engine listings, and then develop a methodology for improving rankings to draw more searchers to their clients' sites. Search engine optimization encompasses both "on page" factors (like body copy, title elements, H1 heading elements and image <a href="/wiki/Alt_attribute" title="Alt attribute">alt attribute</a> values) and Off Page Optimization factors (like <a href="/wiki/Anchor_text" title="Anchor text">anchor text</a> and PageRank). The general idea is to affect Google's relevance algorithm by incorporating the keywords being targeted in various places "on page", in particular the title element and the body copy (note: the higher up in the page, presumably the better its keyword prominence and thus the ranking). Too many occurrences of the keyword, however, cause the page to look suspect to Google's spam checking algorithms. Google has published guidelines for website owners who would like to raise their rankings when using legitimate optimization consultants.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has been hypothesized, and, allegedly, is the opinion of the owner of one business about which there have been numerous complaints, that negative publicity, for example, numerous consumer complaints, may serve as well to elevate page rank on Google Search as favorable comments.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The particular problem addressed in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> article, which involved <a href="/wiki/DecorMyEyes" class="mw-redirect" title="DecorMyEyes">DecorMyEyes</a>, was addressed shortly thereafter by an undisclosed fix in the Google algorithm. According to Google, it was not the frequently published consumer complaints about DecorMyEyes which resulted in the high ranking but mentions on news websites of events which affected the firm such as legal actions against it. <a href="/wiki/Google_Search_Console" title="Google Search Console">Google Search Console</a> helps to check for websites that use duplicate or copyright content.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;Hummingbird&quot;_search_algorithm_upgrade"><span id=".22Hummingbird.22_search_algorithm_upgrade"></span>"Hummingbird" search algorithm upgrade</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Google_Hummingbird" title="Google Hummingbird">Google Hummingbird</a></div>
<p>In 2013, Google significantly upgraded its search algorithm with "Hummingbird". Its name was derived from the speed and accuracy of the <a href="/wiki/Hummingbird" title="Hummingbird">hummingbird</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-What&#95;it&#95;means&#95;for&#95;SEO&#95;46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_it_means_for_SEO-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The change was announced on September 26, 2013, having already been in use for a month.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "Hummingbird" places greater emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Natural_language" title="Natural language">natural language</a> queries, considering context and meaning over individual keywords.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-What&#95;it&#95;means&#95;for&#95;SEO&#95;46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_it_means_for_SEO-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also looks deeper at content on individual pages of a website, with improved ability to lead users directly to the most appropriate page rather than just a website's homepage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The upgrade marked the most significant change to Google search in years, with more "human" search interactions<sup id="cite&#95;ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a much heavier focus on conversation and meaning.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-What&#95;it&#95;means&#95;for&#95;SEO&#95;46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-What_it_means_for_SEO-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Thus, web developers and writers were encouraged to <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_optimization" title="Search engine optimization">optimize their sites</a> with natural writing rather than forced keywords, and make effective use of technical web development for on-site navigation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Search_results_quality">Search results quality</h3></div>
<p>In 2023, drawing on internal Google documents disclosed as part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Google_LLC_(2020)" title="United States v. Google LLC (2020)">United States v. Google LLC (2020)</a> antitrust case, technology reporters claimed that Google Search was "bloated and overmonetized"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and that the "semantic matching" of search queries put advertising profits before quality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i> withdrew Megan Gray's piece after Google complained about alleged inaccuracies, while the author reiterated that «As stated in court, "A goal of Project Mercury was to increase commercial queries"».<sup id="cite&#95;ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2024, Google announced a significant update to its core search algorithm and spam targeting, which is expected to wipe out 40&#160;percent of all spam results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On March 20th, it was confirmed that the roll out of the spam update was complete.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Shopping_search">Shopping search</h3></div>
<p>On September 10, 2024, the European-based <a href="/wiki/EU_Court_of_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="EU Court of Justice">EU Court of Justice</a> found that Google held an illegal monopoly with the way the company showed favoritism to its shopping search, and could not avoid paying €2.4 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-europeanshopping&#95;56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europeanshopping-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The EU Court of Justice referred to Google's treatment of rival shopping searches as "discriminatory" and in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Digital_Markets_Act" title="Digital Markets Act">Digital Markets Act</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-europeanshopping&#95;56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europeanshopping-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Interface">Interface</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Page_layout">Page layout</h3></div>
<p>At the top of the search page, the approximate result count and the response time two digits behind decimal is noted. Of search results, page titles and URLs, dates, and a preview text snippet for each result appears. Along with web search results, sections with images, news, and videos may appear.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The length of the previewed text snipped was experimented with in 2015 and 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Universal_search">Universal search</h3></div>
<p>"Universal search" was launched by Google on May 16, 2007, as an idea that merged the results from different kinds of search types into one. Prior to Universal search, a standard Google search would consist of links only to websites. Universal search, however, incorporates a wide variety of sources, including websites, news, pictures, maps, blogs, videos, and more, all shown on the same search results page.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marissa_Mayer" title="Marissa Mayer">Marissa Mayer</a>, then-vice president of search products and user experience, described the goal of Universal search as "we're attempting to break down the walls that traditionally separated our various search properties and integrate the vast amounts of information available into one simple set of search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, Google expanded its search results to cover available job listings. The data is aggregated from various major job boards and collected by analyzing company homepages. Initially only available in English, the feature aims to simplify finding jobs suitable for each user.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Rich_snippets">Rich snippets</h3></div>
<p>In May 2009, Google announced that they would be parsing website <a href="/wiki/Microformat" title="Microformat">microformats</a> to populate search result pages with "Rich snippets". Such snippets include additional details about results, such as displaying reviews for restaurants and social media accounts for individuals.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, Google expanded on the "Rich snippets" format to offer "Rich cards", which, similarly to snippets, display more information about results, but shows them at the top of the mobile website in a swipeable carousel-like format.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Originally limited to movie and recipe websites in the United States only, the feature expanded to all countries globally in 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Knowledge_Graph">Knowledge Graph</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Graph_(Google)" title="Knowledge Graph (Google)">Knowledge Graph (Google)</a></div>
<p>The Knowledge Graph is a knowledge base used by Google to enhance its search engine's results with information gathered from a variety of sources.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Introducing&#95;the&#95;Knowledge&#95;Graph&#95;68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introducing_the_Knowledge_Graph-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This information is presented to users in a box to the right of search results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Knowledge Graph boxes were added to Google's search engine in May 2012,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Introducing&#95;the&#95;Knowledge&#95;Graph&#95;68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Introducing_the_Knowledge_Graph-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> starting in the United States, with international expansion by the end of the year.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The information covered by the Knowledge Graph grew significantly after launch, tripling its original size within seven months,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and being able to answer "roughly one-third" of the 100 billion monthly searches Google processed in May 2016.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Knowledge&#95;Graph&#95;TWP&#95;72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knowledge_Graph_TWP-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The information is often used as a spoken answer in <a href="/wiki/Google_Assistant" title="Google Assistant">Google Assistant</a><sup id="cite&#95;ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Home_(platform)" title="Google Home (platform)">Google Home</a> searches.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Knowledge Graph has been criticized for providing answers without source attribution.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Knowledge&#95;Graph&#95;TWP&#95;72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knowledge_Graph_TWP-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Google_Knowledge_Panel">Google Knowledge Panel</h3></div>
<p>A Google Knowledge Panel<sup id="cite&#95;ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a feature integrated into Google search engine result pages, designed to present a structured overview of entities such as individuals, organizations, locations, or objects directly within the search interface. This feature leverages data from Google's Knowledge Graph,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a database that organizes and interconnects information about entities, enhancing the retrieval and presentation of relevant content to users.
</p><p>The content within a Knowledge Panel<sup id="cite&#95;ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is derived from various sources, including <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> and other structured databases, ensuring that the information displayed is both accurate and contextually relevant. For instance, querying a well-known public figure may trigger a Knowledge Panel displaying essential details such as biographical information, birthdate, and links to social media profiles or official websites.
</p><p>The primary objective of the Google Knowledge Panel is to provide users with immediate, factual answers, reducing the need for extensive navigation across multiple web pages.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Personal_tab">Personal tab</h3></div>
<p>In May 2017, Google enabled a new "Personal" tab in Google Search, letting users search for content in their Google accounts' various services, including email messages from <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a> and photos from <a href="/wiki/Google_Photos" title="Google Photos">Google Photos</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Google_Discover">Google Discover</h3></div>
<p>Google Discover, previously known as Google Feed, is a personalized stream of articles, videos, and other news-related content. The feed contains a "mix of cards" which show topics of interest based on users' interactions with Google, or topics they choose to follow directly.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Cards include, "links to news stories, YouTube videos, sports scores, recipes, and other content based on what [Google] determined you're most likely to be interested in at that particular moment."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Users can also tell Google they're not interested in certain topics to avoid seeing future updates.
</p><p>Google Discover launched in December 2016<sup id="cite&#95;ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and received a major update in July 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Another major update was released in September 2018, which renamed the app from Google Feed to Google Discover, updated the design, and adding more features.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Discover can be found on a tab in the Google app and by swiping left on the home screen of certain Android devices. As of 2019, Google will not allow <a href="/wiki/Political_campaign" title="Political campaign">political campaigns</a> worldwide to target their advertisement to people to make them vote.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="AI_Overviews">AI Overviews</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AI_Overviews" title="AI Overviews">AI Overviews</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:AI_Overviews_result_for_%22cheese_not_sticking_to_pizza%22,_May_24,_2024.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="&quot;cheese not sticking to pizza&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/AI_Overviews_result_for_%22cheese_not_sticking_to_pizza%22%2C_May_24%2C_2024.jpg/250px-AI_Overviews_result_for_%22cheese_not_sticking_to_pizza%22%2C_May_24%2C_2024.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="231" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/AI_Overviews_result_for_%22cheese_not_sticking_to_pizza%22%2C_May_24%2C_2024.jpg/500px-AI_Overviews_result_for_%22cheese_not_sticking_to_pizza%22%2C_May_24%2C_2024.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="929" data-file-height="857" /></a><figcaption>Early AI Overview response to the problem of "cheese not sticking to pizza"</figcaption></figure>
<p>At the 2023 <a href="/wiki/Google_I/O" title="Google I/O">Google I/O</a> event in May, Google unveiled Search Generative Experience (SGE), an experimental feature in Google Search available through <a href="/wiki/Google_Labs" title="Google Labs">Google Labs</a> which produces <a href="/wiki/AI-generated" class="mw-redirect" title="AI-generated">AI-generated</a> summaries in response to search prompts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was part of Google's wider efforts to counter the unprecedented rise of generative AI technology, ushered by <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>'s launch of <a href="/wiki/ChatGPT" title="ChatGPT">ChatGPT</a>, which sent Google executives to a panic due to its potential threat to Google Search.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google added the ability to generate images in October.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At I/O in 2024, the feature was upgraded and renamed AI Overviews.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-VergeOverviews&#95;88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VergeOverviews-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>AI Overviews was rolled out to users in the United States in May 2024.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-VergeOverviews&#95;88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VergeOverviews-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The feature faced public criticism in the first weeks of its rollout after errors from the tool went viral online. These included results suggesting users add glue to pizza or eat rocks,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BBCMcMahon&#95;89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCMcMahon-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or incorrectly claiming <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> is Muslim.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google described these viral errors as "isolated examples", maintaining that most AI Overviews provide accurate information.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-BBCMcMahon&#95;89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCMcMahon-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two weeks after the rollout of AI Overviews, Google made technical changes and scaled back the feature, pausing its use for some health-related queries and limiting its reliance on social media posts.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i> has criticised the system on environmental grounds, as such a search uses 30 times more energy than a conventional one.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has also been criticized for condensing information from various sources, making it less likely for people to view full articles and websites. When it was announced in May 2024, Danielle Coffey, CEO of the News/Media Alliance was quoted as saying "This will be catastrophic to our traffic, as marketed by Google to further satisfy user queries, leaving even less incentive to click through so that we can monetize our content."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2024, AI Overviews were rolled out in the UK, India, Japan, Indonesia, Mexico and Brazil, with local language support.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On October 28, 2024, AI Overviews was rolled out to 100 more countries, including Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="AI_Mode">AI Mode</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/AI_Mode" class="mw-redirect" title="AI Mode">AI Mode</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1305433154">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output <p>In March 2025, Google introduced an experimental "AI Mode" within its Search platform, enabling users to input complex, multi-part queries and receive comprehensive, AI-generated responses. This feature uses Google's advanced <a href="/wiki/Gemini_(chatbot)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gemini (chatbot)">Gemini</a> 2.0 model, which enhances the system's reasoning capabilities and supports multimodal inputs, including text, images, and voice.
</p><p>Initially, AI Mode was available to <a href="/wiki/Google_One" title="Google One">Google One</a> AI Premium subscribers in the United States, who could access it through the Search Labs platform. This phased rollout allowed Google to gather user feedback and refine the feature before a broader release.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Redesigns">Redesigns</h3></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Product_Sans_typeface_sample.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Product_Sans_typeface_sample.svg/250px-Product_Sans_typeface_sample.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="209" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Product_Sans_typeface_sample.svg/500px-Product_Sans_typeface_sample.svg.png 1.5x" data-file-width="794" data-file-height="663" /></a><figcaption>Product Sans, Google's typeface since 2015</figcaption></figure>
<p>In late June 2011, Google introduced a new look to the Google homepage in order to boost the use of the Google+ social tools.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>One of the major changes was replacing the classic navigation bar with a black one. Google's digital creative director Chris Wiggins explains: "We're working on a project to bring you a new and improved Google experience, and over the next few months, you'll continue to see more updates to our look and feel."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new navigation bar has been negatively received by a vocal minority.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2013, Google started testing yellow labels for advertisements displayed in search results, to improve user experience. The new labels, highlighted in yellow color, and aligned to the left of each sponsored link help users differentiate between organic and sponsored results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On December 15, 2016, Google rolled out a new desktop search interface that mimics their modular mobile user interface. The mobile design consists of a tabular design that highlights search features in boxes and works by imitating the desktop Knowledge Graph real estate, which appears in the right-hand rail of the search engine result page, these featured elements frequently feature Twitter carousels, People Also Search For, and Top Stories (vertical and horizontal design) modules. The Local Pack and Answer Box were two of the original features of the Google <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_results_page" title="Search engine results page">SERP</a> that were primarily showcased in this manner, but this new layout creates a previously unseen level of design consistency for Google results.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-ab&#95;101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ab-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Smartphone_apps">Smartphone apps</h3></div>
<p>Google offers a "Google Search" <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a> for <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> and <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> devices.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The mobile apps exclusively feature Google Discover and a "Collections" feature, in which the user can save for later perusal any type of search result like images, bookmarks or map locations into groups.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Android devices were introduced to a preview of the feed, perceived as related to <a href="/wiki/Google_Now" title="Google Now">Google Now</a>, in December 2016,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> while it was made official on both Android and iOS in July 2017.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2016, Google updated its Search app on Android to feature "Trends"; search queries gaining popularity appeared in the autocomplete box along with normal query autocompletion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The update received significant backlash, due to encouraging search queries unrelated to users' interests or intentions, prompting the company to issue an update with an opt-out option.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2017, the Google Search app on iOS was updated to feature the same functionality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2017, Google released "Google Go", an app designed to enable use of Google Search on physically smaller and lower-spec devices in multiple languages. A Google blog post about designing "India-first" products and features explains that it is "tailor-made for the millions of people in [India and Indonesia] coming online for the first time".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Performing_a_search"><span class="anchor" id="Domain&#95;names"></span>Performing a search</h2></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Google_Search_with_definition_from_Wikipedia_on_the_right_side.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3e/Google_Search_with_definition_from_Wikipedia_on_the_right_side.png/500px-Google_Search_with_definition_from_Wikipedia_on_the_right_side.png" decoding="async" width="340" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/3e/Google_Search_with_definition_from_Wikipedia_on_the_right_side.png 1.5x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>A definition link is provided for many search terms.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Google Search consists of a series of <a href="/wiki/Website_localization" title="Website localization">localized websites</a>. The largest of those, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.google.com/?safe=active&amp;ssui=on">google.com site</a>, is the top most-visited website in the world.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-alexarank&#95;111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexarank-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Some of its features include a definition link for most searches including dictionary words, the number of results you got on your search, links to other searches (e.g. for words that Google believes to be misspelled, it provides a link to the search results using its proposed spelling), the ability to filter results to a date range,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and many more.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Search_syntax">Search syntax<span class="anchor" id="Google&#95;Advanced&#95;Search"></span></h3></div>
<p>Google search accepts queries as normal text, as well as individual keywords.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-How&#95;to&#95;search&#95;113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_to_search-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It <a href="/wiki/Autocorrection" title="Autocorrection">automatically corrects</a> apparent misspellings by default (while offering to use the original spelling as a selectable alternative), and provides the same results regardless of capitalization.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-How&#95;to&#95;search&#95;113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How_to_search-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For more customized results, one can use a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Operator_(computer_programming)" title="Operator (computer programming)">operators</a>, including, but not limited to:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><code>OR</code> or <code>|</code>  – Search for webpages containing one of two similar queries, such as <i>marathon OR race</i></li>
<li><code>AND</code>  – Search for webpages containing two similar queries, such as <i>marathon AND runner</i></li>
<li><code>-</code> (minus sign) – Exclude a word or a phrase, so that <i>"apple -tree"</i> searches where word <i>"tree"</i> is not used
<ul><li><code>-ai</code> – Exclude <a href="/wiki/AI-generated_content" class="mw-redirect" title="AI-generated content">AI-generated content</a> from webpages, including Google AI Overviews.</li></ul></li>
<li><code>""</code> – Force inclusion of a word or a phrase, such as <i>"tallest building"</i></li>
<li><code>*</code> – Placeholder symbol allowing for any substitute words in the context of the query, such as <i>"largest * in the world"</i></li>
<li><code>..</code> – Search within a range of numbers, such as <i>"camera $50..$100"</i></li>
<li><code>site:</code> – Search within a specific website, such as <i>"site:<a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">youtube.com</a>"</i></li>
<li><code>-site:</code> – Do not display search results from within a specific website, such as <i>"-site:<a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">youtube.com</a>"</i></li>
<li><code>define:</code> – Search for definitions for a word or phrase, such as <i>"define:phrase"</i></li>
<li><code>stocks:</code> – See the stock price of investments, such as <i>"stocks:googl"</i></li>
<li><code>related:</code> – Find web pages related to specific <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URL</a> addresses, such as <i>"related:www.wikipedia.org"</i></li>
<li><code>( )</code>  – Group operators and searches, such as <i>(marathon OR race) AND shoes</i></li>
<li><code>filetype:</code>  or <code>ext:</code> – Search for specific file types, such as <i>filetype:gif</i></li>
<li><code>before:</code>  – Search for before a specific date, such as spacex <i>before:2020-08-11</i></li>
<li><code>after:</code>  – Search for after a specific date, such as iphone <i>after:2007-06-29</i></li>
<li><code>@</code> – Search for the search term on a specific social media site, such as <i>"@<a href="/wiki/Twitter" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitter">twitter</a>"</i></li></ul>
<p>Google also offers a <b>Google Advanced Search</b> page with a web interface to access the advanced features without needing to remember the special operators.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2024 Google no longer displays cached versions of webpages.
Previously the command <code>cache:</code> would present a cached version of a webpage with the search term highlighted, e.g. <i>"cache:www.google.com xxx"</i> showed cached content with word "xxx" highlighted.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Unlike other search engines, when searching for exact phrases, Google Search only takes words that are on the same line into account.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Query_expansion">Query expansion</h4></div>
<p>Google applies <a href="/wiki/Query_expansion" title="Query expansion">query expansion</a> to submitted search queries, using techniques to deliver results that it considers "smarter" than the query users actually submitted. This technique involves several steps, including:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Word <a href="/wiki/Stemming" title="Stemming">stemming</a> – Certain words can be reduced so other, similar terms, are also found in results, so that <i>"translator"</i> can also search for <i>"translation"</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">Acronyms</a> – Searching for abbreviations can also return results about the name in its full length, so that <i>"<a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>"</i> can show results for <i>"North Atlantic Treaty Organization"</i></li>
<li>Misspellings – Google will often suggest correct spellings for misspelled words</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Synonym" title="Synonym">Synonyms</a> – In most cases where a word is incorrectly used in a phrase or sentence, Google search will show results based on the correct synonym</li>
<li>Translations – The search engine can, in some instances, suggest results for specific words in a different language</li>
<li>Ignoring words – When search queries contain extraneous or insignificant words, Google search may drop those specific words from the query</li>
<li>Location sensitivity – Google may consider users' geographical location to deliver more relevant results.</li></ul>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:A_screenshot_of_suggestions_by_Google_Search_when_%22wikip%22_is_typed_(new).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/A_screenshot_of_suggestions_by_Google_Search_when_%22wikip%22_is_typed_%28new%29.png/250px-A_screenshot_of_suggestions_by_Google_Search_when_%22wikip%22_is_typed_%28new%29.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="112" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/A_screenshot_of_suggestions_by_Google_Search_when_%22wikip%22_is_typed_%28new%29.png/500px-A_screenshot_of_suggestions_by_Google_Search_when_%22wikip%22_is_typed_%28new%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="1443" data-file-height="648" /></a><figcaption>A screenshot of suggestions by Google Search when "wikip" is typed</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2008, Google started to give users <a href="/wiki/Autocomplete" title="Autocomplete">autocompleted</a> <a href="/wiki/Search_suggest_drop-down_list" title="Search suggest drop-down list">search suggestions</a> in a list below the search bar while typing, originally with the approximate result count previewed for each listed search suggestion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;I'm_Feeling_Lucky&quot;"><span id=".22I.27m_Feeling_Lucky.22"></span>"I'm Feeling Lucky"</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"I'm Feeling Lucky" redirects here. For the 2011 book by Douglas Edwards, see <a href="/wiki/I%27m_Feeling_Lucky_(book)" title="I&#39;m Feeling Lucky (book)"><i>I'm Feeling Lucky</i> (book)</a>.</div>
<p>Google's homepage used to show a button labeled "I'm Feeling Lucky". This feature originally allowed users to type in their search query, click the button and be taken directly to the first result, bypassing the search results page. Clicking it while leaving the search box empty opens Google's archive of <a href="/wiki/Google_Doodle" title="Google Doodle">Doodles</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> With the 2010 announcement of <a href="#Instant_search">Google Instant</a>, an automatic feature that immediately displays relevant results as users are typing in their query, the "I'm Feeling Lucky" button disappears, requiring that users opt-out of Instant results through search settings to keep using the "I'm Feeling Lucky" functionality.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2012, "I'm Feeling Lucky" was changed to serve as an advertisement for Google services; users hover their computer mouse over the button, it spins and shows an emotion ("I'm Feeling Puzzled" or "I'm Feeling Trendy", for instance), and, when clicked, takes users to a Google service related to that emotion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tom_Chavez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tom Chavez (page does not exist)">Tom Chavez</a> of "Rapt", a firm helping to determine a website's advertising worth, estimated in 2007 that Google lost $110 million in revenue per year due to use of the button, which bypasses the advertisements found on the search results page.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_interactive_features">Special interactive features</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Google_Easter_eggs#Embedded_tools" title="List of Google Easter eggs">List of Google Easter eggs §&#160;Embedded tools</a></div>
<p>Besides the main text-based search-engine function of Google search, it also offers multiple quick, interactive features. These include, but are not limited to:<sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span class="anchor" id="calculator"></span><a href="/wiki/List_of_Google_Easter_eggs#Calculator" title="List of Google Easter eggs">Calculator</a></li>
<li>Time zone, currency, and unit conversions</li>
<li>Word translations</li>
<li>Flight status</li>
<li>Local film showings</li>
<li>Weather forecasts</li>
<li>Population and unemployment rates</li>
<li>Package tracking</li>
<li>Word definitions</li>
<li>Metronome</li>
<li>Roll a die</li>
<li>"Do a barrel roll" (search page spins)</li>
<li>"Askew" (results show up sideways)</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="&quot;OK_Google&quot;_conversational_search"><span id=".22OK_Google.22_conversational_search"></span><span class="anchor" id="Conversational&#95;search&#95;(OK&#95;Google)"></span>"OK Google" conversational search</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Google_Now" title="Google Now">Google Now</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Assistant" title="Google Assistant">Google Assistant</a></div>
<p>During Google's developer conference, <a href="/wiki/Google_I/O" title="Google I/O">Google I/O</a>, in May 2013, the company announced that users on <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a> and <a href="/wiki/ChromeOS" title="ChromeOS">ChromeOS</a> would be able to have the browser initiate an audio-based search by saying "OK Google", with no button presses required. After having the answer presented, users can follow up with additional, contextual questions; an example include initially asking "OK Google, will it be sunny in Santa Cruz this weekend?", hearing a spoken answer, and reply with "how far is it from here?"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> An update to the Chrome browser with <a href="/wiki/Voice_search" title="Voice search">voice-search</a> functionality rolled out a week later, though it required a button press on a microphone icon rather than "OK Google" voice activation.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Google released a browser extension for the Chrome browser, named with a "<a href="/wiki/Beta_software" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta software">beta</a>" tag for unfinished development, shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2014, the company officially added "OK Google" into the browser itself;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> they removed it in October 2015, citing low usage, though the microphone icon for activation remained available.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In May 2016, 20% of search queries on mobile devices were done through voice.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Operations">Operations</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Search_products">Search products</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Google_products" title="List of Google products">List of Google products</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Google Videos" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Google_Videos_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Google Videos (disambiguation)">Google Videos (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png/330px-Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="138" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png/500px-Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png/960px-Google_Videos_search_engine_screenshot.png 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="886" /></a></span><div class="infobox-caption">Google Videos homepage as of 2025</div></div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="display: inline-block;
